     255             : /**
     256             :  * \brief Destroy an open GDALDataset.
     257             :  *
     258             :  * This is the accepted method of closing a GDAL dataset and deallocating
     259             :  * all resources associated with it.
     260             :  *
     261             :  * Equivalent of the C callable GDALClose().  Except that GDALClose() first
     262             :  * decrements the reference count, and then closes only if it has dropped to
     263             :  * zero.
     264             :  *
     265             :  * For Windows users, it is not recommended to use the delete operator on the
     266             :  * dataset object because of known issues when allocating and freeing memory
     267             :  * across module boundaries. Calling GDALClose() is then a better option.
     268             :  */

     395             : /************************************************************************/
     396             : /*                             FlushCache()                             */
     397             : /************************************************************************/
     398             : 
     399             : /**
     400             :  * \brief Flush all write cached data to disk.
     401             :  *
     402             :  * Any raster (or other GDAL) data written via GDAL calls, but buffered
     403             :  * internally will be written to disk.
     404             :  *
     405             :  * The default implementation of this method just calls the FlushCache() method
     406             :  * on each of the raster bands and the SyncToDisk() method
     407             :  * on each of the layers.  Conceptionally, calling FlushCache() on a dataset
     408             :  * should include any work that might be accomplished by calling SyncToDisk()
     409             :  * on layers in that dataset.
     410             :  *
     411             :  * Using this method does not prevent use from calling GDALClose()
     412             :  * to properly close a dataset and ensure that important data not addressed
     413             :  * by FlushCache() is written in the file.
     414             :  *
     415             :  * This method is the same as the C function GDALFlushCache().
     416             :  */
     417             :

    1130             : 
    1131             : /**
    1132             :  * \brief Fetch the affine transformation coefficients.
    1133             :  *
    1134             :  * Fetches the coefficients for transforming between pixel/line (P,L) raster
    1135             :  * space, and projection coordinates (Xp,Yp) space.
    1136             :  *
    1137             :  * \code
    1138             :  *   Xp = padfTransform[0] + P*padfTransform[1] + L*padfTransform[2];
    1139             :  *   Yp = padfTransform[3] + P*padfTransform[4] + L*padfTransform[5];
    1140             :  * \endcode
    1141             :  *
    1142             :  * In a north up image, padfTransform[1] is the pixel width, and
    1143             :  * padfTransform[5] is the pixel height.  The upper left corner of the
    1144             :  * upper left pixel is at position (padfTransform[0],padfTransform[3]).
    1145             :  *
    1146             :  * The default transform is (0,1,0,0,0,1) and should be returned even when
    1147             :  * a CE_Failure error is returned, such as for formats that don't support
    1148             :  * transformation to projection coordinates.
    1149             :  *
    1150             :  * This method does the same thing as the C GDALGetGeoTransform() function.
    1151             :  *
    1152             :  * @param padfTransform an existing six double buffer into which the
    1153             :  * transformation will be placed.
    1154             :  *
    1155             :  * @return CE_None on success, or CE_Failure if no transform can be fetched.
    1156             :  */
    1157             : 
    1158        6158 : CPLErr GDALDataset::GetGeoTransform( double * padfTransform )
    1159             : 
    1160             : {
    1161        6158 :     CPLAssert(padfTransform != nullptr);
    1162             : 
    1163        6158 :     padfTransform[0] = 0.0;  // X Origin (top left corner)
    1164        6158 :     padfTransform[1] = 1.0;  // X Pixel size */
    1165        6158 :     padfTransform[2] = 0.0;
    1166             : 
    1167        6158 :     padfTransform[3] = 0.0;  // Y Origin (top left corner)
    1168        6158 :     padfTransform[4] = 0.0;
    1169        6158 :     padfTransform[5] = 1.0;  // Y Pixel Size
    1170             :

    1895             :  * overviews (.ovr), TIFF internal overviews, etc.

    1897             :  * This method is the same as the C function GDALBuildOverviews().

    2330             : /************************************************************************/
    2331             : /*                              RasterIO()                              */
    2332             : /************************************************************************/
    2333             : 
    2334             : /**
    2335             :  * \brief Read/write a region of image data from multiple bands.
    2336             :  *
    2337             :  * This method allows reading a region of one or more GDALRasterBands from
    2338             :  * this dataset into a buffer,  or writing data from a buffer into a region
    2339             :  * of the GDALRasterBands.  It automatically takes care of data type
    2340             :  * translation if the data type (eBufType) of the buffer is different than
    2341             :  * that of the GDALRasterBand.
    2342             :  * The method also takes care of image decimation / replication if the
    2343             :  * buffer size (nBufXSize x nBufYSize) is different than the size of the
    2344             :  * region being accessed (nXSize x nYSize).
    2345             :  *
    2346             :  * The nPixelSpace, nLineSpace and nBandSpace parameters allow reading into or
    2347             :  * writing from various organization of buffers.
    2348             :  *
    2349             :  * For highest performance full resolution data access, read and write
    2350             :  * on "block boundaries" as returned by GetBlockSize(), or use the
    2351             :  * ReadBlock() and WriteBlock() methods.
    2352             :  *
    2353             :  * This method is the same as the C GDALDatasetRasterIO() or
    2354             :  * GDALDatasetRasterIOEx() functions.
    2355             :  *
    2356             :  * @param eRWFlag Either GF_Read to read a region of data, or GF_Write to
    2357             :  * write a region of data.
    2358             :  *
    2359             :  * @param nXOff The pixel offset to the top left corner of the region
    2360             :  * of the band to be accessed.  This would be zero to start from the left side.
    2361             :  *
    2362             :  * @param nYOff The line offset to the top left corner of the region
    2363             :  * of the band to be accessed.  This would be zero to start from the top.
    2364             :  *
    2365             :  * @param nXSize The width of the region of the band to be accessed in pixels.
    2366             :  *
    2367             :  * @param nYSize The height of the region of the band to be accessed in lines.
    2368             :  *
    2369             :  * @param pData The buffer into which the data should be read, or from which
    2370             :  * it should be written.  This buffer must contain at least
    2371             :  * nBufXSize * nBufYSize * nBandCount words of type eBufType.  It is organized
    2372             :  * in left to right,top to bottom pixel order.  Spacing is controlled by the
    2373             :  * nPixelSpace, and nLineSpace parameters.
    2374             :  *
    2375             :  * @param nBufXSize the width of the buffer image into which the desired region
    2376             :  * is to be read, or from which it is to be written.
    2377             :  *
    2378             :  * @param nBufYSize the height of the buffer image into which the desired
    2379             :  * region is to be read, or from which it is to be written.
    2380             :  *
    2381             :  * @param eBufType the type of the pixel values in the pData data buffer. The
    2382             :  * pixel values will automatically be translated to/from the GDALRasterBand
    2383             :  * data type as needed.
    2384             :  *
    2385             :  * @param nBandCount the number of bands being read or written.
    2386             :  *
    2387             :  * @param panBandMap the list of nBandCount band numbers being read/written.
    2388             :  * Note band numbers are 1 based. This may be NULL to select the first
    2389             :  * nBandCount bands.
    2390             :  *
    2391             :  * @param nPixelSpace The byte offset from the start of one pixel value in
    2392             :  * pData to the start of the next pixel value within a scanline. If defaulted
    2393             :  * (0) the size of the datatype eBufType is used.
    2394             :  *
    2395             :  * @param nLineSpace The byte offset from the start of one scanline in
    2396             :  * pData to the start of the next. If defaulted (0) the size of the datatype
    2397             :  * eBufType * nBufXSize is used.
    2398             :  *
    2399             :  * @param nBandSpace the byte offset from the start of one bands data to the
    2400             :  * start of the next. If defaulted (0) the value will be
    2401             :  * nLineSpace * nBufYSize implying band sequential organization
    2402             :  * of the data buffer.
    2403             :  *
    2404             :  * @param psExtraArg (new in GDAL 2.0) pointer to a GDALRasterIOExtraArg
    2405             :  * structure with additional arguments to specify resampling and progress
    2406             :  * callback, or NULL for default behaviour. The GDAL_RASTERIO_RESAMPLING
    2407             :  * configuration option can also be defined to override the default resampling
    2408             :  * to one of BILINEAR, CUBIC, CUBICSPLINE, LANCZOS, AVERAGE or MODE.
    2409             :  *
    2410             :  * @return CE_Failure if the access fails, otherwise CE_None.
    2411             :  */

    2709             : /**

    2712             :  * Some GDAL drivers operate more efficiently if they know in advance what
    2713             :  * set of upcoming read requests will be made.  The AdviseRead() method allows
    2714             :  * an application to notify the driver of the region and bands of interest,
    2715             :  * and at what resolution the region will be read.

    2717             :  * Many drivers just ignore the AdviseRead() call, but it can dramatically
    2718             :  * accelerate access via some drivers.

    2985             : /************************************************************************/
    2986             : /*                              GDALOpen()                              */
    2987             : /************************************************************************/
    2988             : 
    2989             : /**
    2990             :  * \brief Open a raster file as a GDALDataset.
    2991             :  *
    2992             :  * This function will try to open the passed file, or virtual dataset
    2993             :  * name by invoking the Open method of each registered GDALDriver in turn.
    2994             :  * The first successful open will result in a returned dataset.  If all
    2995             :  * drivers fail then NULL is returned and an error is issued.
    2996             :  *
    2997             :  * Several recommendations :
    2998             :  * <ul>
    2999             :  * <li>If you open a dataset object with GA_Update access, it is not recommended
    3000             :  * to open a new dataset on the same underlying file.</li>
    3001             :  * <li>The returned dataset should only be accessed by one thread at a time. If
    3002             :  * you want to use it from different threads, you must add all necessary code
    3003             :  * (mutexes, etc.)  to avoid concurrent use of the object. (Some drivers, such
    3004             :  * as GeoTIFF, maintain internal state variables that are updated each time a
    3005             :  * new block is read, thus preventing concurrent use.) </li>
    3006             :  * </ul>
    3007             :  *
    3008             :  * For drivers supporting the VSI virtual file API, it is possible to open a
    3009             :  * file in a .zip archive (see VSIInstallZipFileHandler()), in a
    3010             :  * .tar/.tar.gz/.tgz archive (see VSIInstallTarFileHandler()) or on a HTTP / FTP
    3011             :  * server (see VSIInstallCurlFileHandler())
    3012             :  *
    3013             :  * In some situations (dealing with unverified data), the datasets can be opened
    3014             :  * in another process through the \ref gdal_api_proxy mechanism.
    3015             :  *
    3016             :  * \sa GDALOpenShared()
    3017             :  * \sa GDALOpenEx()
    3018             :  *
    3019             :  * @param pszFilename the name of the file to access.  In the case of
    3020             :  * exotic drivers this may not refer to a physical file, but instead contain
    3021             :  * information for the driver on how to access a dataset.  It should be in UTF-8
    3022             :  * encoding.
    3023             :  *
    3024             :  * @param eAccess the desired access, either GA_Update or GA_ReadOnly.  Many
    3025             :  * drivers support only read only access.
    3026             :  *
    3027             :  * @return A GDALDatasetH handle or NULL on failure.  For C++ applications
    3028             :  * this handle can be cast to a GDALDataset *.
    3029             :  */
    3030             : 
    3031             : GDALDatasetH CPL_STDCALL

    3042             : /************************************************************************/
    3043             : /*                             GDALOpenEx()                             */
    3044             : /************************************************************************/
    3045             : 
    3046             : /**
    3047             :  * \brief Open a raster or vector file as a GDALDataset.
    3048             :  *
    3049             :  * This function will try to open the passed file, or virtual dataset
    3050             :  * name by invoking the Open method of each registered GDALDriver in turn.
    3051             :  * The first successful open will result in a returned dataset.  If all
    3052             :  * drivers fail then NULL is returned and an error is issued.
    3053             :  *
    3054             :  * Several recommendations :
    3055             :  * <ul>
    3056             :  * <li>If you open a dataset object with GDAL_OF_UPDATE access, it is not
    3057             :  * recommended to open a new dataset on the same underlying file.</li>
    3058             :  * <li>The returned dataset should only be accessed by one thread at a time. If
    3059             :  * you want to use it from different threads, you must add all necessary code
    3060             :  * (mutexes, etc.)  to avoid concurrent use of the object. (Some drivers, such
    3061             :  * as GeoTIFF, maintain internal state variables that are updated each time a
    3062             :  * new block is read, thus preventing concurrent use.) </li>
    3063             :  * </ul>
    3064             :  *
    3065             :  * For drivers supporting the VSI virtual file API, it is possible to open a
    3066             :  * file in a .zip archive (see VSIInstallZipFileHandler()), in a
    3067             :  * .tar/.tar.gz/.tgz archive (see VSIInstallTarFileHandler()) or on a HTTP / FTP
    3068             :  * server (see VSIInstallCurlFileHandler())
    3069             :  *
    3070             :  * In some situations (dealing with unverified data), the datasets can be opened
    3071             :  * in another process through the \ref gdal_api_proxy mechanism.
    3072             :  *
    3073             :  * In order to reduce the need for searches through the operating system
    3074             :  * file system machinery, it is possible to give an optional list of files with
    3075             :  * the papszSiblingFiles parameter.
    3076             :  * This is the list of all files at the same level in the file system as the
    3077             :  * target file, including the target file. The filenames must not include any
    3078             :  * path components, are essentially just the output of VSIReadDir() on the
    3079             :  * parent directory. If the target object does not have filesystem semantics
    3080             :  * then the file list should be NULL.
    3081             :  *
    3082             :  * @param pszFilename the name of the file to access.  In the case of
    3083             :  * exotic drivers this may not refer to a physical file, but instead contain
    3084             :  * information for the driver on how to access a dataset.  It should be in UTF-8
    3085             :  * encoding.
    3086             :  *
    3087             :  * @param nOpenFlags a combination of GDAL_OF_ flags that may be combined
    3088             :  * through logical or operator.
    3089             :  * <ul>
    3090             :  * <li>Driver kind: GDAL_OF_RASTER for raster drivers, GDAL_OF_VECTOR for vector
    3091             :  *     drivers, GDAL_OF_GNM for Geographic Network Model drivers.
    3092             :  *     If none of the value is specified, all kinds are implied.</li>
    3093             :  * <li>Access mode: GDAL_OF_READONLY (exclusive)or GDAL_OF_UPDATE.</li>
    3094             :  * <li>Shared mode: GDAL_OF_SHARED. If set, it allows the sharing of GDALDataset
    3095             :  * handles for a dataset with other callers that have set GDAL_OF_SHARED.
    3096             :  * In particular, GDALOpenEx() will first consult its list of currently
    3097             :  * open and shared GDALDataset's, and if the GetDescription() name for one
    3098             :  * exactly matches the pszFilename passed to GDALOpenEx() it will be
    3099             :  * referenced and returned, if GDALOpenEx() is called from the same thread.</li>
    3100             :  * <li>Verbose error: GDAL_OF_VERBOSE_ERROR. If set, a failed attempt to open
    3101             :  * the file will lead to an error message to be reported.</li>
    3102             :  * </ul>
    3103             :  *
    3104             :  * @param papszAllowedDrivers NULL to consider all candidate drivers, or a NULL
    3105             :  * terminated list of strings with the driver short names that must be
    3106             :  * considered.
    3107             :  *
    3108             :  * @param papszOpenOptions NULL, or a NULL terminated list of strings with open
    3109             :  * options passed to candidate drivers. An option exists for all drivers,
    3110             :  * OVERVIEW_LEVEL=level, to select a particular overview level of a dataset.
    3111             :  * The level index starts at 0. The level number can be suffixed by "only" to
    3112             :  * specify that only this overview level must be visible, and not sub-levels.
    3113             :  * Open options are validated by default, and a warning is emitted in case the
    3114             :  * option is not recognized. In some scenarios, it might be not desirable (e.g.
    3115             :  * when not knowing which driver will open the file), so the special open option
    3116             :  * VALIDATE_OPEN_OPTIONS can be set to NO to avoid such warnings. Alternatively,
    3117             :  * since GDAL 2.1, an option name can be preceded by the @ character to indicate
    3118             :  * that it may not cause a warning if the driver doesn't declare this option.
    3119             :  *
    3120             :  * @param papszSiblingFiles NULL, or a NULL terminated list of strings that are
    3121             :  * filenames that are auxiliary to the main filename. If NULL is passed, a
    3122             :  * probing of the file system will be done.
    3123             :  *
    3124             :  * @return A GDALDatasetH handle or NULL on failure.  For C++ applications
    3125             :  * this handle can be cast to a GDALDataset *.
    3126             :  *
    3127             :  * @since GDAL 2.0
    3128             :  */
    3129             : 
    3130       40056 : GDALDatasetH CPL_STDCALL GDALOpenEx( const char *pszFilename,

    3132             :                                      const char *const *papszAllowedDrivers,

    3137             :

    3139             : /*      In case of shared dataset, first scan the existing list to see  */

    3473             : /************************************************************************/
    3474             : /*                           GDALOpenShared()                           */
    3475             : /************************************************************************/
    3476             : 
    3477             : /**
    3478             :  * \brief Open a raster file as a GDALDataset.
    3479             :  *
    3480             :  * This function works the same as GDALOpen(), but allows the sharing of
    3481             :  * GDALDataset handles for a dataset with other callers to GDALOpenShared().
    3482             :  *
    3483             :  * In particular, GDALOpenShared() will first consult its list of currently
    3484             :  * open and shared GDALDataset's, and if the GetDescription() name for one
    3485             :  * exactly matches the pszFilename passed to GDALOpenShared() it will be
    3486             :  * referenced and returned.
    3487             :  *
    3488             :  * Starting with GDAL 1.6.0, if GDALOpenShared() is called on the same
    3489             :  * pszFilename from two different threads, a different GDALDataset object will
    3490             :  * be returned as it is not safe to use the same dataset from different threads,
    3491             :  * unless the user does explicitly use mutexes in its code.
    3492             :  *
    3493             :  * For drivers supporting the VSI virtual file API, it is possible to open a
    3494             :  * file in a .zip archive (see VSIInstallZipFileHandler()), in a
    3495             :  * .tar/.tar.gz/.tgz archive (see VSIInstallTarFileHandler()) or on a HTTP / FTP
    3496             :  * server (see VSIInstallCurlFileHandler())
    3497             :  *
    3498             :  * In some situations (dealing with unverified data), the datasets can be opened
    3499             :  * in another process through the \ref gdal_api_proxy mechanism.
    3500             :  *
    3501             :  * \sa GDALOpen()
    3502             :  * \sa GDALOpenEx()
    3503             :  *
    3504             :  * @param pszFilename the name of the file to access.  In the case of
    3505             :  * exotic drivers this may not refer to a physical file, but instead contain
    3506             :  * information for the driver on how to access a dataset.  It should be in
    3507             :  * UTF-8 encoding.
    3508             :  *
    3509             :  * @param eAccess the desired access, either GA_Update or GA_ReadOnly.  Many
    3510             :  * drivers support only read only access.
    3511             :  *
    3512             :  * @return A GDALDatasetH handle or NULL on failure.  For C++ applications
    3513             :  * this handle can be cast to a GDALDataset *.
    3514             :  */
    3515             : 
    3516             : GDALDatasetH CPL_STDCALL
    3517        5095 : GDALOpenShared( const char *pszFilename, GDALAccess eAccess )

    3519        5095 :     VALIDATE_POINTER1(pszFilename, "GDALOpenShared", nullptr);

    3652             : /************************************************************************/
    3653             : /*                        BeginAsyncReader()                            */
    3654             : /************************************************************************/
    3655             : 
    3656             : /**
    3657             :  * \brief Sets up an asynchronous data request
    3658             :  *
    3659             :  * This method establish an asynchronous raster read request for the
    3660             :  * indicated window on the dataset into the indicated buffer.  The parameters
    3661             :  * for windowing, buffer size, buffer type and buffer organization are similar
    3662             :  * to those for GDALDataset::RasterIO(); however, this call only launches
    3663             :  * the request and filling the buffer is accomplished via calls to
    3664             :  * GetNextUpdatedRegion() on the return GDALAsyncReader session object.
    3665             :  *
    3666             :  * Once all processing for the created session is complete, or if no further
    3667             :  * refinement of the request is required, the GDALAsyncReader object should
    3668             :  * be destroyed with the GDALDataset::EndAsyncReader() method.
    3669             :  *
    3670             :  * Note that the data buffer (pData) will potentially continue to be
    3671             :  * updated as long as the session lives, but it is not deallocated when
    3672             :  * the session (GDALAsyncReader) is destroyed with EndAsyncReader().  It
    3673             :  * should be deallocated by the application at that point.
    3674             :  *
    3675             :  * Additional information on asynchronous IO in GDAL may be found at:
    3676             :  *   http://trac.osgeo.org/gdal/wiki/rfc24_progressive_data_support
    3677             :  *
    3678             :  * This method is the same as the C GDALBeginAsyncReader() function.
    3679             :  *
    3680             :  * @param nXOff The pixel offset to the top left corner of the region
    3681             :  * of the band to be accessed.  This would be zero to start from the left side.
    3682             :  *
    3683             :  * @param nYOff The line offset to the top left corner of the region
    3684             :  * of the band to be accessed.  This would be zero to start from the top.
    3685             :  *
    3686             :  * @param nXSize The width of the region of the band to be accessed in pixels.
    3687             :  *
    3688             :  * @param nYSize The height of the region of the band to be accessed in lines.
    3689             :  *
    3690             :  * @param pBuf The buffer into which the data should be read. This buffer must
    3691             :  * contain at least nBufXSize * nBufYSize * nBandCount words of type eBufType.
    3692             :  * It is organized in left to right,top to bottom pixel order.  Spacing is
    3693             :  * controlled by the nPixelSpace, and nLineSpace parameters.
    3694             :  *
    3695             :  * @param nBufXSize the width of the buffer image into which the desired region
    3696             :  * is to be read, or from which it is to be written.
    3697             :  *
    3698             :  * @param nBufYSize the height of the buffer image into which the desired
    3699             :  * region is to be read, or from which it is to be written.
    3700             :  *
    3701             :  * @param eBufType the type of the pixel values in the pData data buffer.  The
    3702             :  * pixel values will automatically be translated to/from the GDALRasterBand
    3703             :  * data type as needed.
    3704             :  *
    3705             :  * @param nBandCount the number of bands being read or written.
    3706             :  *
    3707             :  * @param panBandMap the list of nBandCount band numbers being read/written.
    3708             :  * Note band numbers are 1 based.   This may be NULL to select the first
    3709             :  * nBandCount bands.
    3710             :  *
    3711             :  * @param nPixelSpace The byte offset from the start of one pixel value in
    3712             :  * pData to the start of the next pixel value within a scanline.  If defaulted
    3713             :  * (0) the size of the datatype eBufType is used.
    3714             :  *
    3715             :  * @param nLineSpace The byte offset from the start of one scanline in
    3716             :  * pData to the start of the next.  If defaulted the size of the datatype
    3717             :  * eBufType * nBufXSize is used.
    3718             :  *
    3719             :  * @param nBandSpace the byte offset from the start of one bands data to the
    3720             :  * start of the next.  If defaulted (zero) the value will be
    3721             :  * nLineSpace * nBufYSize implying band sequential organization
    3722             :  * of the data buffer.
    3723             :  *
    3724             :  * @param papszOptions Driver specific control options in a string list or NULL.
    3725             :  * Consult driver documentation for options supported.
    3726             :  *
    3727             :  * @return The GDALAsyncReader object representing the request.
    3728             :  */
    3729             : 
    3730           1 : GDALAsyncReader *GDALDataset::BeginAsyncReader(

    3733             :     int nPixelSpace, int nLineSpace, int nBandSpace, char **papszOptions )

    3892             :  * This method should release any reference to other datasets (e.g. a VRT
    3893             :  * dataset to its sources), but not close the current dataset itself.
    3894             :  *
    3895             :  * If at least, one reference to a dependent dataset has been dropped,
    3896             :  * this method should return TRUE. Otherwise it *should* return FALSE.
    3897             :  * (Failure to return the proper value might result in infinite loop)
    3898             :  *
    3899             :  * This method can be called several times on a given dataset. After
    3900             :  * the first time, it should not do anything and return FALSE.
    3901             :  *
    3902             :  * The driver implementation may choose to destroy its raster bands,
    3903             :  * so be careful not to call any method on the raster bands afterwards.
    3904             :  *
    3905             :  * Basically the only safe action you can do after calling
    3906             :  * CloseDependentDatasets() is to call the destructor.

    3909             :  * GDALDriverManager::~GDALDriverManager()

    4232             : /************************************************************************/
    4233             : /*                            CreateLayer()                             */
    4234             : /************************************************************************/
    4235             : 
    4236             : /**
    4237             : \brief This method attempts to create a new layer on the dataset with the
    4238             : indicated name, coordinate system, geometry type.
    4239             : 
    4240             : The papszOptions argument
    4241             : can be used to control driver specific creation options.  These options are
    4242             : normally documented in the format specific documentation.
    4243             : 
    4244             : In GDAL 2.0, drivers should extend the ICreateLayer() method and not
    4245             : CreateLayer().  CreateLayer() adds validation of layer creation options, before
    4246             : delegating the actual work to ICreateLayer().
    4247             : 
    4248             : This method is the same as the C function GDALDatasetCreateLayer() and the
    4249             : deprecated OGR_DS_CreateLayer().
    4250             : 
    4251             : In GDAL 1.X, this method used to be in the OGRDataSource class.
    4252             : 
    4253             : Example:
    4254             : 
    4255             : \code{.cpp}
    4256             : #include "gdal.h"
    4257             : #include "cpl_string.h"
    4258             : 
    4259             : ...
    4260             : 
    4261             :         OGRLayer *poLayer;
    4262             :         char     **papszOptions;
    4263             : 
    4264             :         if( !poDS->TestCapability( ODsCCreateLayer ) )
    4265             :         {
    4266             :         ...
    4267             :         }
    4268             : 
    4269             :         papszOptions = CSLSetNameValue( papszOptions, "DIM", "2" );
    4270             :         poLayer = poDS->CreateLayer( "NewLayer", nullptr, wkbUnknown,
    4271             :                                      papszOptions );
    4272             :         CSLDestroy( papszOptions );
    4273             : 
    4274             :         if( poLayer == NULL )
    4275             :         {
    4276             :             ...
    4277             :         }
    4278             : \endcode
    4279             : 
    4280             : @param pszName the name for the new layer.  This should ideally not
    4281             : match any existing layer on the datasource.
    4282             : @param poSpatialRef the coordinate system to use for the new layer, or NULL if
    4283             : no coordinate system is available.  The driver might only increase
    4284             : the reference counter of the object to take ownership, and not make a full copy,
    4285             : so do not use OSRDestroySpatialReference(), but OSRRelease() instead when you
    4286             : are done with the object.
    4287             : @param eGType the geometry type for the layer.  Use wkbUnknown if there
    4288             : are no constraints on the types geometry to be written.
    4289             : @param papszOptions a StringList of name=value options.  Options are driver
    4290             : specific.
    4291             : 
    4292             : @return NULL is returned on failure, or a new OGRLayer handle on success.

    4451             : /**
    4452             :  \brief Execute an SQL statement against the data store.
    4453             : 
    4454             :  The result of an SQL query is either NULL for statements that are in error,
    4455             :  or that have no results set, or an OGRLayer pointer representing a results

    4464             :  review the <a href="ogr_sql.html">OGR SQL</a> document.  Some drivers (i.e.
    4465             :  Oracle and PostGIS) pass the SQL directly through to the underlying RDBMS.
    4466             : 
    4467             :  Starting with OGR 1.10, the <a href="ogr_sql_sqlite.html">SQLITE dialect</a>
    4468             :  can also be used.

    4475             : 
    4476             :  @param pszDialect allows control of the statement dialect. If set to NULL, the
    4477             :  OGR SQL engine will be used, except for RDBMS drivers that will use their
    4478             :  dedicated SQL engine, unless OGRSQL is explicitly passed as the
    4479             :  dialect. Starting with OGR 1.10, the SQLITE dialect can also be used.
    4480             :

    5882             : /**
    5883             :  \brief Execute an SQL statement against the data store.
    5884             : 
    5885             :  The result of an SQL query is either NULL for statements that are in error,
    5886             :  or that have no results set, or an OGRLayer pointer representing a results
    5887             :  set from the query.  Note that this OGRLayer is in addition to the layers
    5888             :  in the data store and must be destroyed with
    5889             :  ReleaseResultSet() before the dataset is closed
    5890             :  (destroyed).

    5892             :  This method is the same as the C function GDALDatasetExecuteSQL() and the
    5893             :  deprecated OGR_DS_ExecuteSQL().

    5895             :  For more information on the SQL dialect supported internally by OGR
    5896             :  review the <a href="ogr_sql.html">OGR SQL</a> document.  Some drivers (i.e.
    5897             :  Oracle and PostGIS) pass the SQL directly through to the underlying RDBMS.
    5898             : 
    5899             :  Starting with OGR 1.10, the <a href="ogr_sql_sqlite.html">SQLITE dialect</a>
    5900             :  can also be used.
    5901             : 
    5902             :  In GDAL 1.X, this method used to be in the OGRDataSource class.
    5903             : 
    5904             :  @param pszStatement the SQL statement to execute.
    5905             :  @param poSpatialFilter geometry which represents a spatial filter. Can be NULL.
    5906             :  @param pszDialect allows control of the statement dialect. If set to NULL, the
    5907             :  OGR SQL engine will be used, except for RDBMS drivers that will use their
    5908             :  dedicated SQL engine, unless OGRSQL is explicitly passed as the
    5909             :  dialect. Starting with OGR 1.10, the SQLITE dialect can also be used.
    5910             :

    6611             : /************************************************************************/
    6612             : /*                          GetNextFeature()                            */
    6613             : /************************************************************************/
    6614             : 
    6615             : /**
    6616             :  \brief Fetch the next available feature from this dataset.
    6617             : 
    6618             :  This method is intended for the few drivers where OGRLayer::GetNextFeature()
    6619             :  is not efficient, but in general OGRLayer::GetNextFeature() is a more
    6620             :  natural API.
    6621             : 
    6622             :  See GetFeatures() for a C++ iterator version of this method.
    6623             : 
    6624             :  The returned feature becomes the responsibility of the caller to
    6625             :  delete with OGRFeature::DestroyFeature().
    6626             : 
    6627             :  Depending on the driver, this method may return features from layers in a
    6628             :  non sequential way. This is what may happen when the
    6629             :  ODsCRandomLayerRead capability is declared (for example for the
    6630             :  OSM and GMLAS drivers). When datasets declare this capability, it is strongly
    6631             :  advised to use GDALDataset::GetNextFeature() instead of
    6632             :  OGRLayer::GetNextFeature(), as the later might have a slow, incomplete or stub
    6633             :  implementation.
    6634             : 
    6635             :  The default implementation, used by most drivers, will
    6636             :  however iterate over each layer, and then over each feature within this
    6637             :  layer.
    6638             : 
    6639             :  This method takes into account spatial and attribute filters set on layers that
    6640             :  will be iterated upon.
    6641             : 
    6642             :  The ResetReading() method can be used to start at the beginning again.
    6643             : 
    6644             :  Depending on drivers, this may also have the side effect of calling
    6645             :  OGRLayer::GetNextFeature() on the layers of this dataset.
    6646             : 
    6647             :  This method is the same as the C function GDALDatasetGetNextFeature().
    6648             : 
    6649             :  @param ppoBelongingLayer a pointer to a OGRLayer* variable to receive the

    6780             : /************************************************************************/
    6781             : /*                     GDALDatasetGetNextFeature()                      */
    6782             : /************************************************************************/
    6783             : /**
    6784             :  \brief Fetch the next available feature from this dataset.
    6785             : 
    6786             :  This method is intended for the few drivers where OGR_L_GetNextFeature()
    6787             :  is not efficient, but in general OGR_L_GetNextFeature() is a more
    6788             :  natural API.
    6789             : 
    6790             :  The returned feature becomes the responsibility of the caller to
    6791             :  delete with OGRFeature::DestroyFeature().
    6792             : 
    6793             :  Depending on the driver, this method may return features from layers in a
    6794             :  non sequential way. This is what may happen when the
    6795             :  ODsCRandomLayerRead capability is declared (for example for the
    6796             :  OSM and GMLAS drivers). When datasets declare this capability, it is strongly
    6797             :  advised to use GDALDataset::GetNextFeature() instead of
    6798             :  OGRLayer::GetNextFeature(), as the later might have a slow, incomplete or stub
    6799             :  implementation.
    6800             : 
    6801             :  The default implementation, used by most drivers, will
    6802             :  however iterate over each layer, and then over each feature within this
    6803             :  layer.
    6804             : 
    6805             :  This method takes into account spatial and attribute filters set on layers that
    6806             :  will be iterated upon.
    6807             : 
    6808             :  The ResetReading() method can be used to start at the beginning again.
    6809             : 
    6810             :  Depending on drivers, this may also have the side effect of calling
    6811             :  OGRLayer::GetNextFeature() on the layers of this dataset.
    6812             : 
    6813             :  This method is the same as the C++ method GDALDataset::GetNextFeature()
    6814             : 
    6815             :  @param hDS               dataset handle.
    6816             :  @param phBelongingLayer  a pointer to a OGRLayer* variable to receive the
    6817             :                           layer to which the object belongs to, or NULL.
    6818             :                           It is possible that the output of *ppoBelongingLayer
    6819             :                           to be NULL despite the feature not being NULL.
    6820             :  @param pdfProgressPct    a pointer to a double variable to receive the
    6821             :                           percentage progress (in [0,1] range), or NULL.
    6822             :                           On return, the pointed value might be negative if
    6823             :                           determining the progress is not possible.
    6824             :  @param pfnProgress       a progress callback to report progress (for
    6825             :                           GetNextFeature() calls that might have a long
    6826             :                           duration) and offer cancellation possibility, or NULL
    6827             :  @param pProgressData     user data provided to pfnProgress, or NULL
    6828             :  @return a feature, or NULL if no more features are available.
    6829             :  @since GDAL 2.2
    6830             : */

    6942             : /************************************************************************/
    6943             : /*                           StartTransaction()                         */
    6944             : /************************************************************************/
    6945             : 
    6946             : /**
    6947             :  \fn GDALDataset::StartTransaction(int)
    6948             :  \brief For datasources which support transactions, StartTransaction creates a
    6949             : `transaction.
    6950             : 
    6951             :  If starting the transaction fails, will return
    6952             :  OGRERR_FAILURE. Datasources which do not support transactions will
    6953             :  always return OGRERR_UNSUPPORTED_OPERATION.
    6954             : 
    6955             :  Nested transactions are not supported.
    6956             : 
    6957             :  All changes done after the start of the transaction are definitely applied in
    6958             :  the datasource if CommitTransaction() is called. They may be canceled by
    6959             :  calling RollbackTransaction() instead.
    6960             : 
    6961             :  At the time of writing, transactions only apply on vector layers.
    6962             : 
    6963             :  Datasets that support transactions will advertise the ODsCTransactions
    6964             :  capability.  Use of transactions at dataset level is generally preferred to
    6965             :  transactions at layer level, whose scope is rarely limited to the layer from
    6966             :  which it was started.
    6967             : 
    6968             :  In case StartTransaction() fails, neither CommitTransaction() or
    6969             :  RollbackTransaction() should be called.
    6970             : 
    6971             :  If an error occurs after a successful StartTransaction(), the whole transaction
    6972             :  may or may not be implicitly canceled, depending on drivers. (e.g.  the PG
    6973             :  driver will cancel it, SQLite/GPKG not). In any case, in the event of an error,
    6974             :  an explicit call to RollbackTransaction() should be done to keep things
    6975             :  balanced.
    6976             : 
    6977             :  By default, when bForce is set to FALSE, only "efficient" transactions will be
    6978             :  attempted. Some drivers may offer an emulation of transactions, but sometimes
    6979             :  with significant overhead, in which case the user must explicitly allow for
    6980             :  such an emulation by setting bForce to TRUE. Drivers that offer emulated
    6981             :  transactions should advertise the ODsCEmulatedTransactions capability (and not
    6982             :  ODsCTransactions).
    6983             : 
    6984             :  This function is the same as the C function GDALDatasetStartTransaction().
    6985             : 
    6986             :  @param bForce can be set to TRUE if an emulation, possibly slow, of a
    6987             :  transaction
    6988             :                mechanism is acceptable.
    6989             : 
    6990             :  @return OGRERR_NONE on success.
    6991             :  @since GDAL 2.0
    6992             : */
    6993             : 
    6994          37 : OGRErr GDALDataset::StartTransaction( CPL_UNUSED int bForce )
    6995             : {
    6996          37 :     return OGRERR_UNSUPPORTED_OPERATION;
    6997             : }
